7 Chapter Seven: Evaluation of Impacts &
Mitigation Measures
7.1 Impact Identification
472. An environmental impact is defined as any change to an existing condition of the
environment. The IEE study, based on the screening and scoping, review of civil works,
review of similar environmental assessment reports, baseline monitoring, and stakeholder
consultations has identified several environmental impacts that are expected from the
project.
473. Findings of the assessment are presented according to pre-construction, construction,
and operation phases. This chapter describes the source of origin of these impacts,
mitigation measures, and potentiality of the impacts caused by the project both tentatively
during construction and permanently during operation.
7.2 Impact during Pre-Construction Phase
7.2.1 Land Acquisition
Impact Origin
474. The project will be set up at Kalampur, Dhamrai which was a non –agricultural land.
Owned by the project proponent there was no use of agricultural or fisheries or homesteads.
Due to this project, no agricultural, wetland, or homestead land is reduced.
475. So, there is no significant impact on the landscape of the area. The proposed project
didn’t require any relocation of homestead and land acquisition has been done by paying
proper compensation of land to the landowners. There was no cultural, historical, and
aesthetic interest in the project land and no loss of a sensible place. So, the impacts that are
mentioned above are negligible.
Impact Potentiality Level: Minor
Mitigation Measure
476. Affected localities due to project setup should be employed in the project or paid up
with a satisfactory project amount.
7.3 Impact during Construction Phase
7.3.1 Disruption of Earth surface: Site preparation, clearing, and earthworks
Impact Origin
477. The proposed project requires site preparation. The preparation works generally done
during the construction stage includes:
IEE of Karim Tex Ltd.
180 | P a g e
➢ Biomass Removal & Disposal
➢ Property removal
➢ Cut and fill operation
➢ Soil Export and Import
➢ Drainage works etc.
478. The impacts generally arise from the above activities are as follows:
➢ Noise
➢ Fugitive dust
➢ Runoff and flooding
➢ Soil erosion: Land erosion along with the uncovered space due to soil removal and
excavation.
➢ Social concerns
➢ Infrastructure disruption
➢ Safety concerns
479. However, the proposed site is of the nature that it will cause negligible impacts in the
pre-construction stages. The site will require some sand and soil filling. The proposed site
has no homestead land so the impact of property removal activities is negligible.
Impact Potentiality Level: Significant
Mitigation Measures
480. Cutting and filling operation during site preparation was kept minimum. The proponent
has already constructed a proper drainage facility. Regular water sprinkle is being used to
minimize fugitive dust emission. Safe working procedures have been established and
already been implemented on the site. Construction work is undertaken during dry seasons.
The heavy construction equipment operates in the daytime.
7.3.2 Impact on Air Environment
Impact Origin
481. All earthworks construction, site clearing, civil construction, mechanical construction,
handling and stocking of construction materials, dry materials stockpiling, hauling of
materials, and construction of drainage generate dust and affect the local air shed. The air
may be polluted due to dust arising from sand/ earth stockpiles by the wind. Construction
dust is likely to be the most significant direct potential impact on the local community. Dust
mites are a common cause of asthma in children.
482. Carbon dioxide and nitrogen oxides may be emitted from the combustion of petroleum
products in project-related vehicles, machinery, generators, etc. during the construction
period. Their impact on air quality will not be significant as the pollutant emission activities
```
(point and area sources) will be limited within the project boundary and the activities will
```
```
be short-term (only for the construction period).
```
IEE of Karim Tex Ltd.
181 | P a g e
Impact Potentiality Level: Major
Mitigation Measures:
483. This impact may further be minimized by adopting the following mitigation measures:
❖ The sprinkling of water at the construction site and haul roads
❖ Trucks transporting fine materials, soil, and waste to and from the project site will be
covered to reduce the release of dust
❖ Raw materials excavated soil and other debris should be stored under covered sheds
```
❖ Generators, electric cutters, and other equipment to be shut down when not infused;
```
❖ Provision of face masks to workers to minimize inhalation of dust particles
❖ Construction vehicles and machinery should be regularly serviced and checked for
pollution control
❖ Low Sulphur diesel should be used for running construction equipment and vehicles
❖ Air emission monitoring program to be undertaken quarterly by the contractor,
❖ A green buffer will be developed all along the project boundary.
7.3.3 Impact on Water Level
Impact Origin
484. Groundwater will be required for construction activities such as concreting, equipment
cleaning, concrete mixing, curing, etc. Water will also be required for drinking and
sanitation purposes of the construction worker.
485. The groundwater will be extracted through pumps and stored in an enclosed area and
later used during the construction eventually leading to groundwater depletion. Apart from
it, the required amount of water that will be used for drinking purposes will be extracted
from the groundwater source which may also lower the groundwater level.
Impact Potentiality Level: Moderate
Mitigation Measures
486. To reduce the impact on groundwater and surface water level, the project proponent
may adopt the following mitigation measures:
❖ A water trigger nozzle will be used instead of open pipe flow to reduce water wastage
❖ Recycled water should be used for construction equipment cleaning
❖ Awareness will be increased through proper training, monitoring, posturing, and signage.
❖ Increasing water storage in the reservoirs
IEE of Karim Tex Ltd.
182 | P a g e
7.3.4 Impact due to Surface Water Extraction
Impact Origin
487. Surface water may be used for the construction purposes of the dormitory building of
the facility. Moreover, water is also extracted from the pond that is close to the which is
later used for various purposes including the construction.
Impact Potentiality Level: Moderate
Mitigation Measures
488. The following mitigation measures can be adopted
❖ Limit usage of surface water
❖ The pond must be kept clean
❖ Build a barrier around the pond for wastes to enter
7.3.5 Impact on Noise Environment
Impact Origin
489. The operation of different types of machinery and equipment for construction activities
and regular vehicular movement for material and equipment transport may generate noise
during the construction period. The produced noise may have an impact on the existing
acoustic environment. Local inhabitants may feel disturbed due to noise from line sources
```
(traffic movement). Impacts of noise will potentially affect the following.
```
a. Impacts of Noise to Immediate Neighbors
❖ Continuous exposure of neighbors to noise nuisance may result in noise-induced hearing
```
loss;
```
❖ Noise nuisance may reduce the concentration of neighbors
b. Noise Impacts on Employees
❖ The high noise level will force employees to shout loud when communicating with one
```
another;
```
```
❖ Exposure of employees to high noise levels (above 85dB) continuous for 8 hours per
```
```
day may result in noise-induced hearing loss;
```
❖ Exposure of the ear to peak sound level instantaneously may result in deafness.
490. Continuous exposure of neighbors to noise nuisance may result in noise-induced worker
hearing loss. The soil extractor or soil collector truck will movement will be the main source
of noise pollution. Vehicles and machinery may generate noise. However, low-noise
construction vehicles will be used and construction work will not do at night hour.
Moreover, the construction period will be done as soon as possible.
Impact Potentiality Level: Moderate
IEE of Karim Tex Ltd.
183 | P a g e
Mitigation Measures
```
❖ The machinery to be used should comply with the noise standards prescribed by DoE;
```
```
❖ Vehicles and machinery should be regularly serviced and checked for pollution control;
```
```
❖ Employees who work at high noise areas should be provided earplugs;
```
```
❖ No noise-generating activity shall be carried out at the night;
```
❖ No construction activities to be undertaken during night hours to prevent any
```
disturbance to nearby residents and laborers in labor camps;
```
```
❖ Fitting noise machines with noise reduction devices;
```
❖ Temporary noise barriers should be provided near the high noise generating areas like
```
metal or tiles cutting sites, generator rooms, etc.;
```
❖ Any employee who may complain about ear-related pain and or complication while at
```
work to access medical attention at the expense of the contractor or project proponent;
```
❖ Regular noise monitoring.
7.3.6 Impact on Sanitation
Impact Origin
491. The health of the project personnel, construction workers, and laborers living at the
construction site could be impacted if the arrangement of sanitation and drinking water is
not ensured adequately and properly. At a present lot of local laborers are working and in
the future stage of the construction, a lot more will work. They will generate a considerable
amount of human waste. These are the potential source for the spread of diseases, as various
insects will play a dominating role in the spread of diseases. There are chances for the
spread of water-borne diseases also.
Impact Potentiality Level: Moderate
Mitigation Measures
❖ A proper sanitation system has been provided and regular, proper, and safe disposal of
human waste is being ensured.
❖ A sufficient number of drinking water facilities would be provided.
❖ An adequate number of toilets and bathrooms has been made for the workers and a proper
disposal system of sewage waste has been developed.
❖ Necessary awareness and warning sign and the poster has already been installed on the
project site.
7.3.7 Impact on Fossil Fuel depletion
Impact Origin
492. Construction operations consume energy in various forms but have never been
sufficiently accounted for. A considerable portion of energy utilization on construction sites
is associated with the operation of machinery and vehicles for transportation, leveling,
earthworks, lifting, compacting, and mixing. The major forms of energy used in
IEE of Karim Tex Ltd.
184 | P a g e
construction processes on site are diesel, and petrol referred to as fossil fuels. However,
compared to the fossil fuel consumption in the operational phase of the project the amount
is negligible.
Impact Potentiality Level: Moderate
Mitigation Measures
493. The reduction of fossil fuel use in the construction activity should be classified as the
secondary scope of the mitigation as the project manager will not have direct control over
the operation of the construction machinery and process. The contractor will primarily be
responsible for this kind of management. However, some mitigation measures can be taken
like
❖ Preventive maintenance of the machinery
❖ leakage identification to reduce fuel loss
❖ on-site use of secondary containment to reduce fuel spill
❖ Proper training and awareness-raising, posturing, and signage should be provided to the
construction worker and machinery operator
7.3.8 Impact on Occupational Health Safety
Impact Origin
494. Under a controlled situation, an accident is not expected. However, occasionally it
occurs during construction works. An accident may occur during earth cutting, casting,
construction works, and installation of heavy machinery. The protection of the head, eye,
ear, hand, and foot of the workers, laborers, and project personnel could be affected if a
proper and adequate arrangement is not ensured.
Impact Potentiality Level: Minor
Mitigation Measures
```
❖ The workers would wear PPE (Personal Protective Equipment), safety goggles,
```
helmets, vests, and other necessaries.
❖ Health & safety training would be conducted daily and monthly on-site.
❖ The workers and laborers would be made aware of their safety
❖ Ensuring safety measures taken by the on-site workers would be made by the EHS
Manager
7.3.9 Impact due to Odor
Impact Origin
495. The surrounding air will be affected during the construction period as various types of
construction material and works will be held. Many such materials may discharge an
unpleasant odor into the atmosphere causing risks to human health. Waste produced that
IEE of Karim Tex Ltd.
185 | P a g e
will be stored during the construction period may also produce a certain amount of bad
odor which will create a bad atmosphere.
Impact Potentiality Level: Minor
Mitigation Measures
496. To reduce the impact on the atmosphere, the project proponent may adopt the following
mitigation measures:
❖ Cover the drainage system properly
❖ Provide respiratory masks to the workers
❖ Provide a separate waste collection area
❖ Collection of wastes in a segregated form with labeling
❖ Cover the bins properly
❖ Installation of garden pots and small trees
7.3.10 Impact on Natural Drainage
Impact Origin
497. A temporary drainage system will be made during the construction phase for the
discharge of the runoff and domestic waste. It will be connected to the nearby water body.
No damage to the natural drainage system will be made because of the construction of a
new one.
Impact Potentiality Level: Minor
Mitigation Measures
❖ Cover the drainage for less pollution
❖ Proper management of the drainage for less contamination
❖ Site drainage controls to isolate potentially contaminated areas from discharge to the
environment
7.3.11 Impact due to Solid Waste
Impact Origin
498. The proposed project will generate both hazardous and non-hazardous solid waste.
Non-hazardous solid wastes like waste poly, plastic, paper, etc. will be generated from both
the construction and domestic activity. Hazardous wastes may include scrap metal,
chemical drums, chemicals, broken glass, etc. which need to dispose of properly.
Uncontrolled discharge of these wastes will severely damage the soil quality, and water
quality, clog the drainage system as well as damage the natural environment.
Impact Potentiality Level: Moderate
IEE of Karim Tex Ltd.
186 | P a g e
Mitigation Measures
❖ Effective storage facility with protection from rain and leachate generation will be built
```
for both hazardous and non-hazardous waste;
```
```
❖ Solid waste will be stored in the storage area before selling to the authorized third party;
```
❖ Environmental training and awareness programs for tenant workers should be required
7.3.12 Impact on Traffic Safety
Impact Origin
499. Due to the proximity of the location of the proposed project residential area, traffic
safety is one of the most important concerns during the construction phase. Moreover, as
the proposed project is situated just beside the Dhaka-Aricha Highway therefore proximity
of traffic congestion is viable. So, the project proponent has to adopt the required measure.
Impact Potentiality Level: Moderate
Mitigation Measures
❖ Control and monitor the traffic system on the project site
❖ Heavily loaded vehicles shall not be allowed to enter the project area during daytime
❖ Maintain an Internal Traffic Management Plan and update it accordingly.
❖ Maintain a logbook of incoming and outgoing vehicles for construction purposes.
7.3.13 Impact due to Climate Change
500. Many climate stressors are indicated and connected to the project based on the location
of the project. As the project is situated just beside the Dhaka-Aricha Highway, the risk of
flooding is considered as one of the major changes as well as the increase of cyclone and
drought.
501. To mitigate and prevent any further effect on the project, the following mitigation
measures can be adopted by the project proponent.
❖ Proper utilization of the highway
❖ Provide training to all staffs regarding any climate crisis and its mitigation measures.
❖ Prepare an Emergency Preparedness Plan
❖ Conduct regular training and monitoring of the site and maintain EHS activities
7.4 Impact during Operation Phase
7.4.1 Impact on Air Quality
Impact Origin
502. In the operational phase, the project will operate various utility machinery like a
generator, substation for power generation. The emission of exhaust gas from these
machineries may affect the ambient air quality. The situation aggravates when gas contains
IEE of Karim Tex Ltd.
187 | P a g e
a high percentage of impurities like sulfur, hydrocarbon, oxides of nitrogen, particulate
matter, etc. The high temperature of flue gases also impacts the air quality in terms of
thermal pollution. The combustion of fossil fuels inevitably results in the emission of
gaseous pollutants such as sulfur dioxide, oxides of nitrogen, particulate matter, and oxides
of carbon to the atmosphere. The concentration of these emissions is susceptible to
violating the national emission standard and thus considered a significant impact.
Impact Potentiality Level: Major
Mitigation Measures
❖ The latest technology, methodology, and machinery involving minimal air emissions
```
should be adopted by industries;
```
❖ Suitable air pollution control measures like a wet scrubber and particulate filter for the
exhaust system should be taken by the project proponent
❖ Generators should be provided with stacks of adequate height to allow enough dispersion
```
of emission;
```
❖ Air pollution monitoring should be carried out quarterly by all industries to check the air
```
pollution level;
```
```
❖ Preference for the usage of relatively clean fuel like low Sulphur diesel should be explored;
```
❖ Energy conservation will be adopted by adopting the alternative energy options like solar
```
power and other energy-efficient technologies;
```
```
❖ Development of a green belt (3.5 m) all along the project boundary
```
7.4.2 Impact due to Solid Waste
Impact Origin
503. The proposed project will generate both hazardous and non-hazardous solid waste.
Nonhazardous solid wastes like waste poly, plastic, paper, etc. will be generated from both
production and domestic activity. Hazardous wastes may include electrical waste, scrap
metal, broken glass, medical waste, etc. which need to dispose of properly. Uncontrolled
discharge of these wastes will severely damage the soil quality, and water quality, clog the
drainage system as well as damage the natural environment.
Impact Potentiality Level: Moderate
Mitigation Measures
```
❖ Implement the national 3R ((Reduce, Reuse and Recycle) Strategy during the operation
```
```
phase for both solid and liquid waste management;
```
❖ Effective storage facility with protection from rain and leachate generation will be built
```
for both hazardous and non-hazardous waste;
```
```
❖ Solid waste will be stored in the storage area before selling to the authorized third party;
```
❖ Medical waste will be collected, stored, and disposed to the authorized medical waste
```
collector;
```
IEE of Karim Tex Ltd.
188 | P a g e
❖ Site drainage controls to isolate potentially contaminated areas from discharge to the
environment
❖ Environmental training and awareness programs for tenant workers should be required
7.4.3 Impact on Sanitation
Impact Origin
504. The health of the project personnel, workers, and laborers working at the site could be
impacted if the arrangement of sanitation and drinking water is not ensured adequately and
properly. It is estimated that a huge number of workers will be present during the operation
phase. They will generate a considerable amount of human waste. These are the potential
source for the spread of diseases, as various insects will play a dominating role in the spread
of diseases. There are chances for the spread of water-borne diseases also.
Impact Potentiality Level: Moderate
Mitigation Measures
❖ A proper sanitation system to be provided and regular, proper, and safe disposal of human
waste is being ensured.
❖ A sufficient number of drinking water facilities would be provided.
❖ An adequate number of toilets and bathrooms has been made for the workers and a proper
disposal system of sewage waste has been developed.
❖ Necessary awareness and warning sign and the poster has already been installed on the
project site.
7.4.4 Impact on Noise and Vibration
Impact Origin
505. In the operation phase of the project, the noise will be generated from various activities
such as the operation of utility machinery, water pumps, traffic activity, etc. Personnel
mostly working in utility areas would face a higher risk of noise pollution because the noise
level would be higher than the acceptable limit prescribed by the DoE and WHO. The
nearby household will also be affected by the high level of noise.
Impact Potentiality Level: Moderate
Mitigation Measures
506. The following mitigation measures should be taken to prevent noise pollution during
the operation phase:
❖ A separate utility room will be built with an enclosing wall
❖ Generator and pumps should be fitted in an acoustic enclosure to reduce the noise
```
generation;
```
❖ Use of ear-muffs and ear-plugs by industries personnel working in the utility area
IEE of Karim Tex Ltd.
189 | P a g e
❖ Plantation should be developed all along the project boundary to form a natural barrier.
```
This will help in reducing the noise level significantly;
```
❖ Regular noise monitoring, especially at the hospital and residence located close by
7.4.5 Impact Due to Water Extraction
Impact Origin
507. The proposed project will require groundwater for drinking and domestic activity. The
amount of water will be extracted from groundwater source through pumps. The regular
extraction of groundwater will eventually lower the water level.
Impact Potentiality Level: Moderate
Mitigation Measures
508. The following mitigation measures should be taken to reduce the impact of water
extraction during the operation phase:
❖ Water trigger nozzles and low flow water faucets will be installed to reduce wastage of
```
water;
```
```
❖ Reuse treated effluent for car washing, gardening, and road watering purpose;
```
7.4.6 Impact on Fossil Fuel Depletion
Impact Origin
509. In the operation phase of the project, fossil fuels like diesel will be required to operate
utility machinery such as generators, fire pumps, operating machines etc. The use of
electricity will be responsible for the depletion of fossil fuels. Fossil fuel depletion will
eventually lead to greenhouse gas emissions.
Impact Potentiality Level: Moderate
Mitigation Measures
❖ The energy-saving appliance should be installed all over the project instead of
```
conventional electrical appliances;
```
❖ Air to fuel mix ratio should be controlled to improve efficiency and reduce fuel use for
```
generator;
```
```
❖ Solar should be installed to reduce purchased or on-site produced electricity usage;
```
❖ Formal energy conservation should be developed and implemented.
7.4.7 Impact on Occupational Health Safety
Impact Origin
510. In the operation phase of the project, a huge number of people will be employed as
worker and administrative personnel. The workers may face occupational health hazards
IEE of Karim Tex Ltd.
190 | P a g e
including accidents due to machinery, slip-trip-fall, allergy, eye irritation, nasal and lung
cancer, skin disease due to exposure to chemicals, heatstroke, etc. from different
operational processes. The safe and good occupational health status of the employees and
workers is important to ensure better plant operation and maintenance as well as improve
their work efficiency. However, due to the irregular frequency of occurrence, the impact
might consider less significant.
Impact Potentiality Level: Minor
Mitigation Measures
❖ Protective clothing, earplug, helmets, shoes, hand gloves, protective goggles, and
```
accessories will be provided to the workers;
```
❖ Adverse impact on worker’s safety could be minimized through implementing a
```
comprehensive occupational health and safety program;
```
```
❖ A regular medical checkup will the soundness of health of employees and workers;
```
```
❖ Safe drinking water and sufficient sanitation facility will be provided;
```
❖ Sufficient training will be provided to the employees about safe chemical and waste
handling, machine operation, firefighting, etc.
7.4.8 Impact on Traffic Safety
Impact Origin
511. Due to the proximity of the residential area, traffic safety is one of the most important
concerns during the operation phase. So, KTL has to adopt some measures.
Impact Potentiality Level: Moderate
Mitigation Measures
❖ to involve community representatives in traffic safety strategy
❖ it includes awareness-raising about how to respond in case of various options
❖ speed hump, traffic barriers, change of road surface, etc. including engineering
measures.
❖ regularly evaluate the accident record, the status of effectiveness of adopted
❖ measures and overall co-operation from the respective community
7.4.9 Impact due to Seismic Risk
Impact Origin
512. The project is located at the Seismic Zone of II according to BNBC 2020. The project
area is likely to be riskier to seismicity and holds major value.
Impact Potentiality Level: Minor
Mitigation Measures
❖ The project shall be built following the Bangladesh National Building Code 2020.
IEE of Karim Tex Ltd.
191 | P a g e
❖ All safety precautions shall be kept in mind while constructing the project
❖ Safety training to be provided to the workers and employees on seismic severity.
7.4.10 Impact due to Flood Risk
Impact Origin
513. As the proposed project will be established just beside the Dhaka-Aricha Highway
therefore the risk of flood in the project area is low. Moreover, the proposed project is
situated in a “Low River Flood” Zone10
Impact Potentiality Level: Minor
Mitigation Measures
❖ Proper safety and barrier to be made during the project construction
7.4.11 Impact on Biodiversity
Impact Origin
514. The construction and maintenance of the factory infrastructure, including the pond, can
result in habitat disruption for various flora and fauna. This may lead to changes in the
distribution of species and even local extinctions. Increased human activities associated
with the factory, such as transportation and waste disposal, can indirectly impact the
surrounding biodiversity. Habitat fragmentation and disturbance from human presence can
lead to changes in the behavior of local wildlife.
Impact Potentiality Level: Moderate
Mitigation Measures
❖ Potential impacts to vegetation, wetlands, fisheries, birdlife, and other sensitive aquatic and
near-shore habitat habitats during operation should be fully assessed with special
consideration for areas of high biodiversity value or those required for the survival of
```
critically endangered or endangered flora and fauna;
```
❖ The depth of the project should be considered at the design phase in terms of habitat
destruction and the amount and nature of dredging required.
7.4.12 Impact on Socio-Economic
515. The proposed project will contribute to covering the increasing demand for yarn which
```
is a beneficial operation factor. Site development will not lead to the loss of any jobs;
```
instead, will create new job opportunities for the local workers.
516. On the other hand, during the construction activities of KTL, jobs and income
opportunities will be created and as such per capita income will be enhanced in this area.
10 Flood Prone Area Map
IEE of Karim Tex Ltd.
192 | P a g e
For operation, several long-term skilled and unskilled personnel will be required which will
create employment opportunities for the local inhabitants also.
517. Since there was no habitation located inside the proposed site, resettlement would not
be necessary for the project. But migration will be increased due to the creation of new job
opportunities in the plant area.
518. People in the neighborhood are expected to get benefit from the employment that would
be generated and from the increased business activities during the construction period.
There is no religious, cultural, or historic place near the site, so the noise and air pollution
during the construction of the project would not create any potential impact. People of the
surrounding area will be benefited from the development of local small businesses due to
the increase in migration in the area.
7.4.13 Impact due to Climate Change
519. The overall climate change variables will be taken into consideration during operation
phases. More important to the climate change stressors such as flood, cyclone, river level
rise will be given to prevent any kind of further damage.
520. The following mitigation measures can be considered during the operation phase
❖ Construct interior barriers to stop low level floodwater from entering basements.
❖ Seal walls in basements with waterproofing compounds to avoid seepage.
❖ Installation of rock beams, rock rip-raps, sand bags,
❖ Maintenance of normal slopes with vegetation or application of soil cements on steeper
slopes
❖ Construction or expansion of drainage
❖ Ventilate with fans or use dehumidifiers to dry out interior spaces.
❖ Quickly remove standing water and water damaged materials. Protect your property
from further damage by boarding up windows and salvaging undamaged items.
7.5 Beneficial Impacts and Enhancement
7.5.1 During Construction
Impact Origin
521. During the construction period, the project will create job opportunities for skilled,
semi-skilled, and unskilled laborers. However, the impact will be a relatively short
duration, being restricted locally to the construction period. Although the numbers of
people who benefited in this way are relatively small, the impacts on individuals can be
disproportionately high compared to the other local people.
IEE of Karim Tex Ltd.
193 | P a g e
Benefit Enhancement Measure
522. Although labor recruitment is a matter of the construction contractor who has the right
to determine whom he shall not employ, still the project proponent shall encourage the
contractor to hire local people wherever possible and to give preference to the employment
of the landless people.
7.5.2 During Operation Phase
Impact Origin
523. The most significant positive impact of the project would be the producing export
quality yarn. The other important positive impact of the project would be the employment
of personnel for the operation of the industry. The project envisages employing an
undetermined number of skilled and unskilled personnel during its operational phase. Apart
from the positive impacts, other beneficial impacts include benefits to the local economy
due to employment, community development, etc.
Benefit Enhancement Measure
524. Although labor recruitment is a matter of the project proponent who has the right to
determine whom he shall and shall not employ, still the project proponent might take
initiative to employ local people wherever possible and to give preference to employment
of the jobless people.
7.6 Decommissioning
7.6.1 General Principles for Environmental Management during Decommissioning
525. At this point of the project planning process, the necessity for and timing of the
decommissioning of the project is unknown. Therefore, only general principles of
decommissioning are detailed below. These principles must be required to be revisited and
supplemented in the event of decommissioning of the project.
526. On decommissioning of the project, the project proponent will:
❖ Ensure that all non-vegetated areas of the project site get vegetated with species
appropriate to the area as soon as possible after the finishing of decommissioning
operation.
❖ All structures, foundations, concrete, and tarred areas are demolished and removed and
waste material is disposed of at an appropriately licensed waste disposal site.
❖ All-access/service roads not required to be retained by landowners are closed and
rehabilitated.
❖ All disturbed areas are compacted, sloped, and contoured to ensure drainage and runoff
and to minimize the risk of erosion.
❖ All hazardous materials should be kept separate, documented, and disposed to a safe
recycling or disposal site.
IEE of Karim Tex Ltd.
194 | P a g e
8 Chapter Eight: Environmental & Social
Management Plan
8.1 General Considerations
527. The Environmental & Social Management Plan (ESMP) is the synthesis of all proposed
mitigation and monitoring actions, set to a time frame with specific responsibility assigned
and follow-up actions defined. ESMP is a plan of action for avoidance, mitigation, and
management of the negative impacts of the project. Environmental & Social enhancement
is also an important component of ESMP. A detailed set of mitigation measures have been
compiled given the likely impacts associated with the development of the proposed project.
528. The ESMP consists of a set of mitigation, monitoring and institutional measures to be
taken during the design, construction, and operation stages of the project. The ESMP has
been designed keeping in view the regulatory and other requirements to ensure the
```
following:
```
```
a) Minimum disturbance to the native flora and fauna
```
```
b) Compliance with the air, water, soil, and noise level norms
```
```
c) Conservation of water and energy to the extent possible.
```
8.2 Mitigation Plan
529. The proposed project may have some impacts on the environment and society which
are identified in previous sections of this report. An Environmental and Social Management
Plan along with Health & Safety Plan has been drafted. Details of which are given below.
The implementation of the ESMP shall be the responsibility of Karim Tex Ltd. who will
intern to implement a part of it through the contractor.

8.3 Enhancement Plan
8.3.1 Introduction:
531. Karim Tex Ltd. in Dhamrai recognizes the importance of environmental sustainability
and is committed to contributing to the local ecosystem. The tree plantation plan aims to
enhance greenery, improve air quality, and promote biodiversity in and around the factory
premises.
8.3.2 Objectives:
532. The main objectives of the tree plantation plan are
❖ Enhance the aesthetic appeal of the factory surroundings.
❖ Offset carbon emissions and improve air quality.
❖ Contribute to local biodiversity conservation.
❖ Engage employees and the local community in environmental initiatives.
8.3.3 Plantation Details:
```
Location:
```
533. The entrance as well as empty spaces can be used for plantation. Moreover, sidewalks
and sides of the production area can be used. Furthermore, the guest house and dormitory
can also be used for tree plantation. The spaces will be benefited from shade, windbreaks,
or aesthetic enhancement.
Species Selection:
534. The selection of species will be such that are native to the region, well-suited to local
soil and climate conditions, and provide ecological benefits. Some suitable species for
Bangladesh include:
```
❖ Mango (Mangifera indica): Provides shade and fruit.
```
```
❖ Neem (Azadirachta indica): Known for its medicinal properties.
```
```
❖ Bamboo (Various species): Fast-growing and versatile.
```
```
❖ Jackfruit (Artocarpus heterophyllus): Large, shade-providing tree with edible fruit.
```
8.3.4 Responsibilities:
535. The responsibilities associated with the tree plantation plan will be divided among the
factory management as well as employees. Moreover, the local community will also be
encouraged to participate in it. The overall responsibilities are provided below.
Factory Management:
❖ Oversee the implementation of the tree plantation plan.
❖ Allocate resources and ensure coordination with relevant stakeholders.
IEE of Karim Tex Ltd.
203 | P a g e
```
Employees:
```
❖ Participate in tree planting activities.
❖ Support maintenance efforts, such as watering and weeding.
Local Community:
❖ Encourage community involvement in tree planting events.
8.3.5 Maintenance Arrangements:
536. For the maintenance and for seeking of the trees and vegetation the following will be
adopted.
❖ Watering: Designate a schedule for regular watering, especially during the dry season.
❖ Weeding: Establish a routine for weeding to ensure the healthy growth of planted trees.
❖ Monitoring: Assign personnel to monitor the health of the trees and address any issues
promptly.
8.3.6 Budget Estimate:
537. An estimated budget for the tree plantation initiative, including costs for tree saplings
procurement, soil preparation and fertilization, watering equipment and outreach and
awareness programs. An Estimation cost of 10-15% of the total budget that has been
allocated for the project can be used for tree plantation. The total cost of the project has
```
been estimated at BDT 8,658,591 in ’000’ (including IDCP) therefore an estimated amount
```
of Taka 1039030.92 can be allocated for the Tree Plantation.
8.3.7 Timeline:
538. For the tree plantation it can be covered over a period of three to six months which will
be accumulated over the construction period. Moreover, some tree plantation can be done
in the operation period as well.
8.3.8 Reporting and Evaluation:
539. Regular reporting on the progress of the tree plantation plan, including the survival rate
of planted trees and any challenges faced will be made. Karim Tex Ltd. is committed to
the successful implementation of the tree plantation plan and looks forward to the positive
environmental impact it will bring to the local community.
8.4 Monitoring Plan
540. The objective of environmental monitoring during the construction and operation
phases is to compare the monitored data against the baseline condition collected during the
study period to assess the effectiveness of the mitigation measures and the protection of the
ambient environment based on national standards. A monitoring schedule has been
developed based on the environmental components that may be affected during the
construction and operation of the project is given below in Table-47.

8.6 Institutional strengthening and training requirements
543. KTL recognizes the paramount importance of institutionalizing effective practices in
```
environmental health and safety (EHS) for the proposed project. To achieve this, an
```
```
Environment, Health & Safety (EHS) Team will be established, headed by a senior
```
management professional equivalent to the Manager. This dedicated team will spearhead
the management of all environmental-related activities, ensuring compliance with
regulations and fostering a culture of safety and sustainability. The organizational structure,
depicted in the organogram, outlines key roles such as the Environmental Coordinator,
Health & Safety Manager, and more. Each team member will be assigned specific
responsibilities to contribute to the overall success of the project. This robust institutional
framework is designed to systematically address environmental challenges, enhance safety
measures, and uphold the organization's commitment to environmental responsibility.
544. As part of our commitment to institutional strengthening, KTL acknowledges the
necessity of comprehensive training programs to equip contractors, workers, and facility
managers with the skills and knowledge essential for effective project execution. These
training initiatives will cover diverse aspects of environmental health, safety protocols,
compliance requirements, and sustainable practices. The associated costs for these training
programs will be meticulously outlined in our budget, ensuring transparency and
accountability. By investing in the continuous development of our workforce, KTL aims
to fortify institutional capacities, guarantee the seamless implementation of environmental
and safety measures, and cultivate a workforce that actively contributes to the sustainability
goals of the proposed project.

below.

9 Chapter Nine: Emergency Response and
Disaster Management Plan
9.1 Emergency Response Plan
547. The initial response to an incident is a critical step in the overall emergency
response. Like all other industries, KTL must have adequate measures against accidents
or incidents to meet the emergency. The purpose of having an Emergency Response Plan
```
(ERP) is to:
```
❖ Assist personnel in determining the appropriate response to emergencies.
❖ Provide personnel with established procedures and guidelines.
❖ Notify the appropriate Emergency Response Team personnel and regulatory/
Govt. agencies.
❖ Manage public and media relations.
❖ Notify the next-to-skin of accident victims.
❖ Promote inter-departmental communications to ensure a “Companywide” Co-
ordinated emergency response.
❖ Minimize the effects that disruptive events can have on company operations by
reducing recovery times and costs.
❖ Respond to immediate requirements to safeguard the subtending environment
and community.
548. This plan covers a range of potential emergencies, including but not limited to
❖ Natural Hazard
❖ Man-made Hazard
❖ Accidents
549. The Emergency Response Procedure will identify who does what and when in the event
of an emergency. Responsibility for who is in charge and their coordination of emergency
actions shall be identified. Nature of Emergency & Hazardous Situations may be of any
or all of the following categories:
I. Emergency
❖ Fire
❖ Explosion
❖ Medical Emergency
❖ Fuel Spill
❖ Failure Of Sewerage System
II. Natural Disasters
❖ Flood
❖ Earthquake/Cyclone
IEE of Karim Tex Ltd.
212 | P a g e
❖ Storm
❖ Cloud Burst Lightning
III. External Factors
❖ Food poisoning/water poisoning
❖ Sabotage
❖ War
9.1.1 Six Steps in Emergency Response
I. Step 01:
```
a) KTL will determine the potential hazards associated with the incident, substance, or
```
circumstances and take appropriate action, identify the type and qualities of
dangerous goods involved and any known associated hazards.
```
b) KTL will identify the potential hazards stemming from local conditions such as
```
inclement weather and water bodies etc. and ensure that the initial response team is
aware of these conditions.
II. Step 02: The Emergency Response Team (ERT) will determine the source/ cause
of the event resulting in the emergency and prevent further losses.
III. Step 03: The ERT will conduct an assessment of the incident site for any further
information on hazards or remedies.
IV. Step 04: The ERT will initiate redresses procedures according to the Grievance
Redress Mechanism and
V. Step 05: The ERT will report the incidence, its nature, cause, the impact applied
redresses procedures, and any further assistance required, etc. to its supervisor or
team leader.
VI. Step 06: The ERT will take appropriate steps concerning hazards to wildlife, and
other resources and address public and media concerns and issues, as applicable.
9.1.2 Reporting Incidents and Accidents
550. All accidents and near-miss incidents shall be investigated to determine what caused
the problem and what action is required to prevent a recurrence. Employees required to
perform investigations shall be trained in accident investigation techniques. The
incident/accident investigation should be a fact-finding exercise rather than faultfinding.
The investigations will focus on the collection of evidence to find out the “root cause” of
the incident. The recommendations of the investigation report are implemented in phases.
IEE of Karim Tex Ltd.
213 | P a g e
9.1.3 Approaches to Emergency Response
551. The main emergency response systems should be in place to deal with dangerous goods
uncontrolled releases of dust, handling of yarn rolls, any kind of injury or medical
emergency while working in the factory and delivery of finished goods, natural calamities,
fires burn, and injuries. The ERP will be trained on specific contingency plans, and
incidence-specific equipment packages in place to cope with these types of emergencies.
In case of an emergency, an incident occurs, immediate action will be taken to mitigate the
impacts. The Emergency Preparedness Policy and Contingency Plan have been appended
in the Annexure Y and Z.
552. To minimize the possibility of injury to the responders and others emergency the EPT
must follow a specific sequence of actions as stepped out in the preceding paragraphs.
9.1.4 Emergency Response Team
553. Different emergency response teams have been established based on four (04) different
```
shifts (A, B, C and General) to strategically coordinate the response to any emergency
```
promptly following the emergency response steps mentioned above. The Emergency
Response team, communication flow, and the responsibilities are described below:
Central Emergency Response
Team
Rescue TeamFirst Aid TeamFire Fighting Team Security Team
IEE of Karim Tex Ltd.
214 | P a g e
Table 50: Responsibilities of the Emergency Response Team
Function Responsibilities
Central Emergency
Response Team ❖ Overall led and coordinated the emergency response and liaised withofficers from government agencies like fire service, DoE, etc.
Fire Fighting Team
❖ Prompt response during fire emergency to extinguish the fire
❖ Maintain communication with the local fire service office
❖ Regular inspection of firefighting equipment
❖ Conduct a regular fire drill
❖ Support training department to conduct training on fire emergency
First Aid Team
❖ provide first aid within the facility to all persons when required
❖ undertake quarterly checks of first aid kit including disposing of
expired items in a safe manner
❖ A response along with the firefighting and rescue team during an
emergency
❖ assist with any incident investigations and unresolved issues related
to health and safety
❖ Maintain liaison with a nearby hospital
Rescue Team
❖ Rescuing and protecting people in the event of emergencies
❖ Conduct regular drills on rescue activity
❖ Support training department to provide general rescue knowledge on
the employee
Security Team
❖ Ensure all personnel understands individual and collective
responsibilities for safety and security.
❖ Liaise with the local security authority
❖ Monitor the operational environment concerning the increased level
of threat and advise the management.
❖ Ensure all interested personnel is kept advised of changes and
threats to the security of project staff, assets, and operations.

9.2 Disaster Management Plan
556. In the normal operation of the project, when all environmental protection equipment
works according to design specification, then there would be no environmental problems
```
for the present project. Disaster (to a certain degree) may occur if the environmental
```
protection equipment fails to work in normal conditions. This situation may arise for any
of the following causes-
❖ If anytime project runs an abnormal situation e.g., if the engines give unwanted noise
than the normal level
❖ If liquid waste overflows and pollutes the surroundings
557. Therefore, an appropriate management plan should have to be taken by the project
proponent to prevent any unwanted disaster in the project. In this regard, there would be a
provision to stop the whole facility immediately during any process failure as discussed
above.
558. The disaster management plan would consist of preventive measures including, among
others, the following.
```
Formulation and strict implementation of safety codes and measures;
```
```
Preventive maintenance;
```
Aware the workers of electric shock
Declaring the project area, a “no smoking zone”
Mock drills by the firefighting cells/ groups
Provision and inspection of firefighting equipment and fire hydrant system in all the
```
sections;
```
```
Proper training of the employees about the importance of codes;
```
Training the employees and the residents of the surrounding about the actions to be taken
during an accident, disaster, etc.
IEE of Karim Tex Ltd.

documentation for ease of accessing information. Some of these documents include:
```
✓ Emergency contacts;

✓ Emergency response procedures for fires
560. The facility's operations and monitoring are carried out under the management and help
from both the employees and relevant government lead agencies. To take care of any
hazards the following control should be adopted:
➢ All safety precautions and provisions cover the general cleanliness of the entire facility
down to, ventilation, lighting, sanitary, waste collection, first aid box provision,
adequate fire extinguishers, and site security by fencing.
9.3 Site Specific Occupational Health and Safety Plan
9.3.1 Importance
561. The Occupational Health and Safety Management Plan (OHSP) is crucial for the project
to ensure the safety and well-being of workers, nearby residents, and the general public.
Here are some of the key reasons why OHSP is important for the Construction phase:
❖ Prevention of accidents and injuries: The project involve heavy machinery,
dangerous equipment, and hazardous materials that can pose a risk to workers and
the public. An OHSP helps to identify and assess potential hazards and develop
strategies to mitigate or eliminate them, thus reducing the risk of accidents and
IEE of Karim Tex Ltd.
223 | P a g e
injuries.
❖ Compliance with legal and regulatory requirements: The project is subject to
various legal and regulatory requirements, including health and safety standards.
An OHSP helps to ensure compliance with these requirements and avoid any legal
or regulatory consequences.
❖ Management of risks and liabilities: The project involve significant risks and
liabilities that can result in financial losses or legal consequences. An OHSP helps
to manage these risks and liabilities by identifying and assessing potential hazards
and implementing strategies to mitigate or eliminate them.
❖ Protection of workers and nearby residents: The project activities will take place
in or near residential areas, which can put nearby residents at risk. An OHSP helps
to protect these residents by implementing measures to minimize noise, dust, and
other disturbances.
❖ Reputation and community relations: The project will have a significant impact
on local communities, and poor health and safety practices can damage an
organization's reputation and community relations. An OHSP helps to demonstrate
a commitment to the safety and well-being of workers and the public, which can
enhance an organization's reputation and community relations.
9.3.2 Objectives and Scope
562. The project proponent is obliged to implement all reasonable precautions to protect the
health and safety of workers and nearby community. This Occupational Health and Safety
Management Plan is aimed at eliminating the occupational hazards, controlling the hazard
at its source through use of engineering controls and minimizing the hazard through design
of safe work systems and administrative or institutional control measures and additional
```
measures of providing appropriate personal protective equipment (PPE) in supplemented
```
by training in the use, and maintenance of the PPE.
563. The plan covers all the aspects of the construction of the proposed project, all works
sited and the facilities of the KTL that are operated in relation to the construction of the
project.
IEE of Karim Tex Ltd.
224 | P a g e

9.3.4 Training
564. All Project workers will undergo HSE knowledge training prior to start of work with
the proposed project.The training will cover HSE management system, operation procedure
training, HSE risk andprevention measures in working areas, correct wearing of protection
articles, usage of special personal protection equipment.
565. The project proponent will conduct at least one occupation health training per month.
All equipment operators and drivers must have training with certificates and will be tested
prior to assignment. The health and safety training will be done through formal training
sessions, HSE induction, toolbox talks, training and awareness and daily pre-start meetings.
Training and induction of workers will include topics such as, but not limited to the

10 Chapter Ten: Stakeholder Consultation
10.1 General
567. Stakeholder or public consultation is a means of involving all primary and secondary
stakeholders in the project’s decision-making process to address their concerns, improve
project design, and give the project legitimacy. Stakeholder consultation, if conducted in a
participatory and objective manner, is a means of enhancing project sustainability.
```
Community input (both knowledge and values) on socio-economic and environmental
```
issues can greatly enhance the quality of decision-making.
568. Stakeholder consultation was therefore conducted in the project area not only to satisfy
the legal requirements of the IEE process in Bangladesh but also to improve and enhance
the social and environmental design of the project.
569. For this section, public participation & community consultation was conducted inside
the premises as well as in the adjacent areas.
10.2 Objectives of Stakeholders Consultation
570. The process of public participation and consultation was endorsed in the United Nations
```
Conference on the Environment and Development (UNCED) in 1992 through one of the
```
key documents of the conference Agenda 21. Agenda 21 is a comprehensive strategy for
global action on sustainable development and deals with issues regarding humanitarian
action with the environment. It emphasizes the role of public participation in environmental
decision-making for the achievement of sustainable development.
571. For projects that have environmental and social impacts, consultation is not a single
conversation but a series of opportunities to create understanding about the project among
those it will likely affect or interest, and to learn how these external parties view the project
and its attendant risks, impacts, opportunities, and mitigation measures.
572. Listening to stakeholder concerns and feedback can be a valuable source of information
that can improve project design and outcomes and help a company to identify and control
external risks. It can also form the basis for future collaboration and partnerships.
573. For stakeholders, a company’s consultation process is an opportunity to get
information, as well as to educate company staff about the local context in which a project
will take place, to raise issues and concerns, ask questions, and potentially help shape the
project by making suggestions for the company to consider and respond to.
574. Through the public consultation process, KTL hopes to:
```
❖ Promote a better understanding of the project, its objective, and its likely impact;
```
```
❖ Identify and address concerns of all interested and affected parties of the project area;
```
❖ Provide a means to identify and resolve issues before plans are finalized and development
```
commences, thus avoiding public anger and resentment and potentially costly delays;
```
❖ Encourage transparency and inculcate trust among various stakeholders to promote
cooperation and partnership with the communities and local leadership.
IEE of Karim Tex Ltd.
229 | P a g e
10.3 Consultation Process
575. Primary stakeholders were consulted during informal and formal meetings held in the
project area. The consultation process was carried out in the Bangla language. During these
meetings, a simple, non-technical, description of the project was given, with an overview
of the project’s likely human and environmental impact. This was followed by an open
discussion allowing participants to voice their concerns and opinions. In addition to
providing communities with information on the proposed project, their feedback was
documented during the primary stakeholder consultation. The issues and suggestions raised
were recorded in field notes for analysis and interpretation.
576. By reaching out to a wider segment of the population and using various communication
tools such as participatory needs assessment, community consultation meetings, focus
group discussions, in-depth interviews, and participatory rural appraisal IEE involved the
community in active decision-making. This process will continue even after this IEE has
been submitted, as well as during future IEEs in which similar tools will be used to create
consensus among stakeholders on specific environmental and social issues in the context
of a proposed project.
577. Secondary stakeholder consultation includes face-to-face meetings and telephonic
conversations with representatives of local government offices, welfare organizations,
NGOs, and nearby hospitals. They were briefed on the IEE process, the project design and
function, and the potential negative and positive impact of the project on the area’s
environment and communities.
578. It was important not to raise community expectations unnecessarily or unrealistically
during the stakeholder consultation meetings to avoid undue conflict with local leaders or
local administrators. The issues recorded in the consultation process were examined,
validated, and addressed in the IEE report.
10.4 Stakeholder Consultation Technique
579. In recognition of the diversity of views within any community, it is very important to
obtain a clear understanding of the different stakeholders and to analyze their capacity and
willingness to be involved in some or all of the project and its planning process. It is also
important to examine how community skills, resources, and ‘local knowledge can be
applied to improve project design and implementation. All of this can be achieved by
careful use of the various tools of Stakeholder Consultation. Therefore, the following
participatory techniques were employed during stakeholder consultations:
❖ Informal meetings and interviews with communities in surrounding areas.
❖ Focus Groups with women, elders, and men participants in the surrounding areas.
IEE of Karim Tex Ltd.
230 | P a g e
10.5 Stakeholder Consulted
580. In the consultation process for IEE, the following key stakeholders were consulted:
❖ Workers present within the facility
❖ Local communities, men, women, and local elders attended meetings.
❖ Local Government representative
581. Meetings with stakeholders consisted of community consultation meetings, focus group
discussions, and in-depth interviews with men. The location of the meetings, the process
followed, and the outcomes are discussed in this section.
10.6 Questionnaire of the Consultation
582. The following questions were asked to conduct the public consultation. And their
feedback is added to Annexure F. The images of the questionnaire survey are mentioned
in Annexure.
Questions
Do you know what kind of factory is being constructed here?
What do you think about the employment opportunity this industry will create?
What do you think about the environmental impacts this industry will generate?
Do you think this industry will develop the surrounding area?
What is your opinion on the establishment of the project?
Do you face any problems due to the construction of the project?

(ii) A new or updated IEE and corrective action plan prepared during project implementation,
```
```
if any; and
```
```
(iii) The environmental monitoring reports.
```
IEE of Karim Tex Ltd.

11 Chapter Eleven: Grievance Redress Mechanism
11.1 Grievance Redress Mechanism
596. The objective of a grievance redress mechanism is to ensure all comments and
complaints from any project stakeholders, including local/regional authorities, residents of
nearby residential areas, employees, and other interested parties are acknowledged and
responded to within a reasonable timeframe.
597. KTL will accept all comments and complaints associated with the project. The
comments and complaints will be summarized and listed in a Complaints/Comments Log
Book. Any person or organization may send comments and/or complaints in person or via
post, email, or facsimile using the contact information.
598. All comments and complaints will be responded to either verbally or in writing, in
accordance with the preferred method of communication specified by the complaint in the
Comments and Complaints Form. All grievances will be registered and acknowledged
within 5 days and responded to within 20 working days. KTL will keep a grievance log
and report on grievance management, as part of half-yearly project progress reports,
available on the KTL website and requested at the project office.
599. The steps involved in the grievances handling procedure are.
```
1) Acknowledge Dissatisfaction
```
```
2) Define the Problem
```
```
3) Identify and Collect the Facts
```
```
4) Carry out Analyze and Decide
```
```
5) Timely Action
```
```
6) Taking Decision
```
```
7) Implementing the Decision
```
```
8) Follow up Action
```
```
9) Review and Modification, if Need be
```
```
10) Arbitration.
```
```
11) An illustration of the grievance redress mechanism is stated below.
```
IEE of Karim Tex Ltd.

11.3 Resources and Responsibilities
602. To ensure proper care on grievances raised by stakeholders the resource and
responsibilities are to be allocated in two levels as mentioned in the following sections:
11.3.1 Site Level Resource and Responsibilities
603. Management of KTL will have dedicated persons to play the role of Stakeholder’s
Liaison Officer at the site. He will have the overall responsibility for handling the
consultation and information disclosure process, including:
❖ Organization of consultation process
❖ Communication with identified stakeholder groups
❖ Collecting and processing comments/complaints
❖ Responding to any such comments and complaints, and
❖ Depending on the nature of a comment/complaint, some comments/complaints will be
provided to the appropriate person in the company for a response.
11.3.2 Corporate Level Resource and Responsibilities
604. A senior representative from KTL will play the role as required at the corporate level
in dealing with addressing stakeholder consultation. He/She is expected to review the
findings/observations and forward them to the corporate level and who will be responsible
for implementing the decisions.
IEE of Karim Tex Ltd.
236 | P a g e
11.4 Reporting
605. There is a requirement for two tiers of reporting as discussed briefly in the following
section.
11.4.1 Internal Reporting
606. Local reporting relevant to the stakeholder’s engagement will be undertaken under the
corporate Communication Programme. At a corporate level, stakeholders’ engagement will
be reported in Annual Reports and other relevant corporate documentation along with
```
provision for grievance box (transparent). A transparent grievance box will be placed
```
within site and reviewed daily.
607. Management reporting on the stakeholder’s engagement will take place through the
Stakeholder’s Liaison Officer. The Corporate Communication Manager will receive a
quarterly report on engagement activities.
11.4.2 External Reporting
608. External Reporting means the reporting requirement for the external client including
funding agency, government and other regulatory bodies, and so on. KTL will provide
stakeholders' Engagement reports to them according to their requirements of them. The
Corporate Communication Manager is expected to manage the external reporting
requirement also and install a grievance box at the main gate of the factory which will be
monitored daily.
IEE of Karim Tex Ltd.
237 | P a g e
12 Chapter Twelve: Conclusion
12.1 Conclusion
609. An Initial Environmental Examination (IEE) study has been carried out for the
proposed project according to the requirement of the DoE and IDCOL for necessary
environmental clearances. The IEE has been prepared by identifying the potential impacts,
assessing them, and recommending possible mitigation and enhancing measures for
negative and positive impacts, respectively. While impact assessment, minimal negative
environmental impacts on location, planning, design, construction, and operation are
anticipated, mostly during the construction and operation of the project.
610. Proper maintenance of the machinery could reduce the emission of air pollutants. Based
on the environmental assessment and surveys conducted for the project, associated
potential adverse environmental impacts can be mitigated to an acceptable level by the
adequate implementation of the measures as stated in the IEE. Adequate provisions should
be made in the project to cover the environmental mitigation and monitoring requirements,
and their associated costs. The possible environmental impacts caused by the operation of
the project may be the noise of the marine vehicles and operational equipment. In addition,
there is an issue of limited SOx emission due to diesel-fouled operational devices like
cranes, excavators, generators and the health safety of the community due to trucks, Lorries,
```
and covered vans. Since it is understood that the project proponent (KTL) is committed to
```
taking the necessary steps to address any environmental problems, the selected location
seems to be acceptable for the proposed project.
611. The findings of this IEE suggest that the project involves some environmental impacts
```
(mostly localized in nature) to which further careful attention should be given to the
```
operation and maintenance of the Project to minimize/mitigate and offset the adverse
effects. The possible negative impacts are not severe, and the adverse impacts if duly
addressed, as stated in the ESMP, could be minimized without much effort, though they
would require attention and positive commitment from the plant management.
612. The location of the project is environmentally in an advantageous condition as has
already been mentioned. However, adequate and effective pollution prevention, abatement,
and control measure, proper and careful operation and maintenance, regular and effective
environmental monitoring with adequate staff and budgetary provision, and reporting to
DoE and IDCOL, should be ensured.
613. However, no development can be expected without any adverse impact on the
environment. The beneficial impacts on the nation, as well as human beings, would only
be meaningful and sustainable development would only be possible if the adverse effects
are minimized through strict maintenance and control measures as adopted and further
suggested for this project.
IEE of Karim Tex Ltd.
238 | P a g e
614. Finally, it can be concluded that the location of the project is environmentally
acceptable and it is expected that the project proponent will follow all environmentally
compatible steps during construction and operation which it sets a positive example as an
environment-friendly industrial facility. No follow-up study would be required for the
proposed project and Environmental Clearance Certificate could be issued in favor of the
project.
12.2 Recommendations
615. Recommendations made for the project development based on the IEE study are given
```
below:
```
❖ The proposed environment management plan should be implemented strictly in both
the operation and construction phase.
❖ Production and utility operations should be conducted using eco-friendly materials.
❖ ODS emitting machinery or substances should be avoided.
❖ The provision of green belt development and segregated stormwater drainage should
have been adhered to.
❖ A waste management system should be developed by implementing a national 3R
strategy.
❖ Proper training in maintaining the environment, health, and safety should be given to
the project management unit in both the construction and operation phases.
❖ The project manager needs to put in place corporate social responsibility projects such
as supporting primary and secondary education in the nearby location.
❖ The Environmental Health and Safety system should be upgraded continuously with
further production expansion to maintain sustainable development.
❖ Traffic management should be monitored and proper mitigation measures should be
taken accordingly.
❖ Regular road watering/spraying should be done and ensured by the EHS head to reduce
the dust emission as much as possible.
❖ Monthly health inspections and training as per the training calendar should be
conducted and maintained by KTL.
```
❖ Proper use of PPEs (helmet, safety shoe, mask, etc) and their implementation should be
```
made sure.
❖ Raw materials should be covered during the transportation and import of it.
❖ An On-site, emergency response team should be present.
IEE of Karim Tex Ltd.
